     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_radio_programs_not_affiliated_with_NPR">
       Public radio programs not affiliated with NPR
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=NPR&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Public radio programs not affiliated with NPR">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Individual NPR stations can broadcast programming from sources that have no formal affiliation with NPR. If these programs are distributed by another distributor, a public radio station must also affiliate with that network to take that network's programming.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Way_With_Words" title="A Way With Words">
         A Way With Words
        </a>
       </i>
       , a show about language; produced by Wayword LLC
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ask_Dr._Science" title="Ask Dr. Science">
         Ask Dr. Science
        </a>
       </i>
       , nonsequitur science humor
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">
         BBC World Service
        </a>
       </i>
       , world news produced by the
       <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">
        BBC
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       , distributed by
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Radio_International" title="Public Radio International">
        Public Radio International
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Earth_%26_Sky" title="Earth &amp; Sky">
         Earth &amp; Sky
        </a>
       </i>
       , a clear voice for science, nature and people in a complex world, hosted by Deborah Byrd and Joel Block
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Echoes_(radio_program)" title="Echoes (radio program)">
         Echoes
        </a>
       </i>
       , a daily program of ambient, new age, and electronic music hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/John_Diliberto" title="John Diliberto">
        John Diliberto
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Forum_(KQED)" title="Forum (KQED)">
         Forum
        </a>
       </i>
       , call-in panel discussion program, wide-ranging national and local topics hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Krasny_(talk_show_host)" title="Michael Krasny (talk show host)">
        Michael Krasny
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/KQED-FM" title="KQED-FM">
        KQED-FM
       </a>
       ).
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Hearts_of_Space" title="Hearts of Space">
         Hearts of Space
        </a>
       </i>
       , a weekly program of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ambient_Music" title="Ambient Music">
        Ambient
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Space_music" title="Space music">
        Space
       </a>
       , and contemplative music hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Hill_(broadcaster)" title="Stephen Hill (broadcaster)">
        Stephen Hill
       </a>
       , San Rafael, Calif.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jazz_from_Lincoln_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jazz from Lincoln Center (page does not exist)">
         Jazz from Lincoln Center
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wynton_Marsalis" title="Wynton Marsalis">
        Wynton Marsalis
       </a>
       , hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/Ed_Bradley" title="Ed Bradley">
        Ed Bradley
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Murray_Street_Productions&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Murray Street Productions (page does not exist)">
        Murray Street Productions
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_Merrow_Report&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The Merrow Report (page does not exist)">
         The Merrow Report
        </a>
       </i>
       , education issues hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/John_Merrow" title="John Merrow">
        John Merrow
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Learning_Matters_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Learning Matters Inc. (page does not exist)">
        Learning Matters Inc.
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_People%27s_Pharmacy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The People's Pharmacy (page does not exist)">
         The People's Pharmacy
        </a>
       </i>
       , a call-in and interview program on personal health from
       <a href="/wiki/WUNC_(FM)" title="WUNC (FM)">
        WUNC
       </a>
       in Chapel Hill, N.C.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_Talk" title="Philosophy Talk">
         Philosophy Talk
        </a>
       </i>
       , everyday topics examined through a philosophical lens, hosted by Stanford philosophy professors
       <a href="/wiki/John_Perry_(philosopher)" title="John Perry (philosopher)">
        John Perry
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Allen_Taylor" title="Kenneth Allen Taylor">
        Ken Taylor
       </a>
       , produced by
       <a href="/wiki/Ben_Manilla" title="Ben Manilla">
        Ben Manilla
       </a>
       Productions.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Planetary_Radio" title="Planetary Radio">
         Planetary Radio
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">
        space exploration
       </a>
       radio program hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/Mat_Kaplan" title="Mat Kaplan">
        Mat Kaplan
       </a>
       , The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Planetary_Society" title="Planetary Society">
        Planetary Society
       </a>
       , Pasadena, Calif.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Pulse_of_the_Planet" title="Pulse of the Planet">
         Pulse of the Planet
        </a>
       </i>
       , a daily 2-minute sound portrait of Planet Earth, hosted by Jim Metzner.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Radio_Reader" title="The Radio Reader">
         The Radio Reader
        </a>
       </i>
       , readings of recently released books
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Science_Friday" title="Science Friday">
         Science Friday
        </a>
        ,
       </i>
       science issues call-in hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/Ira_Flatow" title="Ira Flatow">
        Ira Flatow
       </a>
       and independently produced, distributed by
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Radio_International" title="Public Radio International">
        Public Radio International
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Selected_Shorts" title="Selected Shorts">
         Selected Shorts
        </a>
       </i>
       , dramatic readings hosted by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isaiah_Sheffer" title="Isaiah Sheffer">
        Isaiah Sheffer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Symphony_Space" title="Symphony Space">
        Symphony Space
       </a>
       , (
       <a href="/wiki/WNYC" title="WNYC">
        WNYC
       </a>
       ) and distributed by
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Radio_International" title="Public Radio International">
        Public Radio International
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Serial_(podcast)" title="Serial (podcast)">
         Serial
        </a>
       </i>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">
        podcast
       </a>
       exploring a nonfiction story over
       <a href="/wiki/Serial_(radio_and_television)" title="Serial (radio and television)">
        multiple episodes
       </a>
       .
       <i>
        Serial
       </i>
       is a
       <a href="/wiki/Spin-off_(media)" title="Spin-off (media)">
        spin-off
       </a>
       from
       <i>
        This American Life
       </i>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Takeaway" title="The Takeaway">
         The Takeaway
        </a>
       </i>
       , a daily news program hosted by John Hockenberry and distributed by
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Radio_International" title="Public Radio International">
        Public Radio International
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/StarDate_(radio)" title="StarDate (radio)">
         StarDate
        </a>
       </i>
       , short segments relating to science and astronomy from the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">
        University of Texas at Austin
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/McDonald_Observatory" title="McDonald Observatory">
        McDonald Observatory
       </a>
       hosted by Sandy Wood.
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sunday_Baroque&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sunday Baroque (page does not exist)">
         Sunday Baroque
        </a>
       </i>
       , baroque and early music hosted by Suzanne Bona (
       <a href="/wiki/WSHU-FM" title="WSHU-FM">
        WSHU-FM
       </a>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/This_American_Life" title="This American Life">
         This American Life
        </a>
       </i>
       , stories of real life hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/Ira_Glass" title="Ira Glass">
        Ira Glass
       </a>
       , distributed by
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Radio_Exchange" title="Public Radio Exchange">
        Public Radio Exchange
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/WireTap_(radio_program)" title="WireTap (radio program)">
         WireTap
        </a>
       </i>
       , comedy radio program hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Goldstein_(author)" title="Jonathan Goldstein (author)">
        Jonathan Goldstein
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/CBC_Radio_One" title="CBC Radio One">
        CBC Radio One
       </a>
       and distributed by
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Radio_International" title="Public Radio International">
        Public Radio International
       </a>
       in the United States.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.witsradio.org/" rel="nofollow">
        <i>
         Wits
        </i>
       </a>
       , a sketch comedy, music, and artist interview program, hosted by
       <a href="/wiki/John_Moe" title="John Moe">
        John Moe
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Many shows produced or distributed by Public Radio International—such as
      <i>
       This American Life
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Living_on_Earth" title="Living on Earth">
        Living on Earth
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Feldman%27s_Whad%27Ya_Know%3F" title="Michael Feldman's Whad'Ya Know?">
        Whad'Ya Know?
       </a>
      </i>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Public_Radio" title="Wisconsin Public Radio">
       Wisconsin Public Radio
      </a>
      —are broadcast on public radio stations, but are not affiliated with NPR. PRI and NPR are separate production and distribution organizations with distinct missions, and each competes with the other for programming slots on public radio stations.
     </p>
     <p>
      Public Radio Exchange also offers a national distribution network where a significant number of public radio stations go to acquire programs from independent producers. PRX provides a catalog of thousands of radio pieces available on-demand as broadcast quality audio files and available for streaming on the PRX.org website.
     </p>
     <p>
      Most public radio stations are NPR member stations and affiliate stations of PRI, APM, and PRX
      <i>
       at the same time
      </i>
      . The organizations have different governance structures and missions and relationships with stations. Other popular shows, like
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Prairie_Home_Companion" title="A Prairie Home Companion">
        A Prairie Home Companion
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Marketplace_(radio_program)" title="Marketplace (radio program)">
        Marketplace
       </a>
      </i>
      , are produced by American Public Media, the national programming unit of
      <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Public_Radio" title="Minnesota Public Radio">
       Minnesota Public Radio
      </a>
      . These programs were distributed by Public Radio International prior to APM's founding.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Now!" title="Democracy Now!">
        Democracy Now!
       </a>
      </i>
      , the flagship news program of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacifica_Radio" title="Pacifica Radio">
       Pacifica Radio
      </a>
      network, provides a feed to NPR stations, and other Pacifica programs can occasionally be heard on these stations as well.
     </p>
     <p>
      Additionally, NPR member stations distribute a series of podcast-only programs, such as
      <i>
       Planet Money
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       On Gambling with Mike Pesca
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Groove Salad
      </i>
      , and
      <i>
       Youthcast
      </i>
      , which are designed for younger audiences.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">
       Controversies
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=NPR&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Controversies">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote" role="note">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/NPR_controversies" title="NPR controversies">
       NPR controversies
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Over the course of NPR's history, controversies have arisen over several incidents and topics.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_ideological_bias">
       Allegations of ideological bias
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=NPR&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Allegations of ideological bias">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      NPR has been accused of displaying both liberal bias, as alleged in work such as a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA">
       UCLA
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/University_of_Missouri" title="University of Missouri">
       University of Missouri
      </a>
      study of
      <i>
       Morning Edition
      </i>
      , and conservative bias, including criticism of alleged reliance on conservative
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Think-tank" title="Think-tank">
       think-tanks
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OTM_Bias_58-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-OTM_Bias-58">
        [58]
       </a>
      </sup>
      NPR has also been accused of bias related to specific topics, including support of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2003_Invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 Invasion of Iraq">
       2003 Invasion of Iraq
      </a>
      and coverage of
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israel
      </a>
      . The NPR ombudsman has described how NPR's coverage of the Israel-Palestinian conflict has been simultaneously criticized as biased by both sides.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        [59]
       </a>
      </sup>
      University of Texas journalism professor and author
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Jensen" title="Robert Jensen">
       Robert Jensen
      </a>
      has criticized NPR as taking a pro-war stance during coverage of Iraq war protests.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
       <a href="#cite_note-60">
        [60]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2002 and 2003, surveys and follow-up focus groups conducted by the Tarrance Group and Lake Snell Perry &amp; Associates have indicated that, "The majority of the U.S. adult population does not believe that the news and information programming on public broadcasting is biased. The plurality of Americans indicate that there is no apparent bias one way or the other, while approximately two-in-ten detect a liberal bias and approximately one-in-ten detect a conservative bias."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        [61]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Euphemisms">
       Euphemisms
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=NPR&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Euphemisms">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In a controversial act, NPR banned in 2009 the use of the word "torture" in the context of the Bush administration's use of
      <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_interrogation_techniques" title="Enhanced interrogation techniques">
       enhanced interrogation techniques
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        [62]
       </a>
      </sup>
      NPR's Ombudswoman
      <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Shepard" title="Alicia Shepard">
       Alicia Shepard
      </a>
      's defense of the policy was that "calling waterboarding torture is tantamount to taking sides."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        [63]
       </a>
      </sup>
      But
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UC_Berkeley_School_of_Information" title="UC Berkeley School of Information">
       Berkeley
      </a>
      Professor of Linguistics,
      <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Nunberg" title="Geoffrey Nunberg">
       Geoffrey Nunberg
      </a>
      pointed out that virtually all media around the world, other than what he called the "spineless U.S. media", call these techniques torture.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        [64]
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        [65]
       </a>
      </sup>
      In an article which criticized NPR and other U.S. media for their use of euphemisms for torture,
      <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Greenwald" title="Glenn Greenwald">
       Glenn Greenwald
      </a>
      discussed what he called the enabling "corruption of American journalism":
     </p>
     <blockquote>
      <p>
       This active media complicity in concealing that our Government created a systematic torture regime, by refusing ever to say so, is one of the principal reasons it was allowed to happen for so long. The steadfast, ongoing refusal of our leading media institutions to refer to what the Bush administration did as "torture" – even in the face of more than 100 detainee deaths; the use of that term by a leading Bush official to describe what was done at Guantanamo; and the fact that media outlets frequently use the word "torture" to describe exactly the same methods when used by other countries --reveals much about how the modern journalist thinks.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Live_from_Death_Row_commentaries">
       <i>
        Live from Death Row
       </i>
       commentaries
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=NPR&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Live from Death Row commentaries">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 1994, NPR arranged to air, on
      <i>
       All Things Considered
      </i>
      , a series of three-minute commentaries by
      <a href="/wiki/Mumia_Abu-Jamal" title="Mumia Abu-Jamal">
       Mumia Abu-Jamal
      </a>
      , a journalist convicted in a controversial trial of murdering a
      <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Police_Department" title="Philadelphia Police Department">
       Philadelphia Police
      </a>
      officer. They cancelled airing them after the
      <a href="/wiki/Fraternal_Order_of_Police" title="Fraternal Order of Police">
       Fraternal Order of Police
      </a>
      and members of the U.S. Congress objected.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WaPoAbul-Jamal_67-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WaPoAbul-Jamal-67">
        [67]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Juan_Williams_comments">
       Juan Williams comments
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=NPR&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Juan Williams comments">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On October 20, 2010, NPR terminated Senior News Analyst
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_Williams" title="Juan Williams">
       Juan Williams
      </a>
      's independent contract
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WilliamsIndep_68-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WilliamsIndep-68">
        [68]
       </a>
      </sup>
      over a series of incidents culminating in remarks he made on the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_News_Channel" title="Fox News Channel">
       Fox News Channel
      </a>
      regarding Muslims.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ronald_Schiller_comments">
       Ronald Schiller comments
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=NPR&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Ronald Schiller comments">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In March 2011, conservative political activist and provocateur
      <a href="/wiki/James_O%27Keefe" title="James O'Keefe">
       James O'Keefe
      </a>
      sent partners Simon Templar (a
      <a href="/wiki/Pen_name" title="Pen name">
       pen name
      </a>
      ) and Shaughn Adeleye
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nprexec_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nprexec-69">
        [69]
       </a>
      </sup>
      to secretly record their discussion with
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ronald_Schiller&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ronald Schiller (page does not exist)">
       Ronald Schiller
      </a>
      , NPR's outgoing senior vice president for
      <a href="/wiki/Fundraising" title="Fundraising">
       fundraising
      </a>
      , and an associate, in which Schiller made remarks viewed as disparaging of "the current Republican party, especially the
      <a href="/wiki/Tea_Party_movement" title="Tea Party movement">
       Tea Party
      </a>
      ", and controversial comments regarding Palestine and funding for NPR. NPR disavowed Schiller's comments. CEO Vivian Schiller, who is not related to Ronald, later resigned over the fallout from the comments and the previous firing of Juan Williams.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        [70]
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

          <q>
           Heard by 13.3 million people on 814 radio stations each week, All Things Considered is one of the most popular programs in America.

        <span class="reference-text">
         <cite class="citation news">
          Steinberg, Jacques (November 7, 2003).
          <a class="external text" href="http://query.nytimes.com/gst/fullpage.html?res=9E04EFD81439F934A35752C1A9659C8B63&amp;sec=&amp;spon=&amp;pagewanted=all" rel="nofollow">
           "Billions and Billions Served, Hundreds of Millions Donated"
          </a>
          .
          <i>
           New York Times
          </i>
          <span class="reference-accessdate">
           . Retrieved
           <span class="nowrap">
            July 28,
           </span>
           2008
          </span>
          .
          <q>
           National Public Radio announced yesterday that it had received a bequest worth at least $200 million from the widow of the longtime chairman of the McDonald's restaurant chain. The gift is the largest in the 33-year history of NPR, the nonprofit broadcasting corporation – and about twice the size of NPR's annual operating budget. It is believed to be among the largest ever pledged to an American cultural institution.
          </q>
         </cite>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">
       Further reading
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=NPR&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Further reading">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Gibson, George H.
       <i>
        Public Broadcasting: The Role of the Federal Government, 1919–1976
       </i>
       (Praeger Publishers, 1977).
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780030228315">
        ISBN 9780030228315
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">
        OCLC
       </a>
       <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/3167293" rel="nofollow">
        3167293
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       McCauley, Michael P.
       <i>
        NPR: The Trials and Triumphs of National Public Radio
       </i>
       (Columbia University Press, 2005).
       <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780231121606">
        ISBN 9780231121606
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">
        OCLC
       </a>
       <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/937175101" rel="nofollow">
        937175101
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Magee, Sara.
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.tandfonline.com/doi/full/10.1080/19376529.2013.823970" rel="nofollow">
        "
        <i>
         All Things Considered
        </i>
        : A Content Analysis of National Public Radio's Flagship News Magazine from 1999–2009"
       </a>
       .
       <i>
        Journal of Radio &amp; Audio Media
       </i>
       (2013) 20#2 pp. 236–250.
      </li>
